<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Conversion of units</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note"><span class="plainlinks selfreference noprint">For the conversion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MOS:CONVERSIONS" title="MOS:CONVERSIONS">units on Wikipedia</a>, see <a href="/wiki/Template:Convert" title="Template:Convert">Template:Convert</a></span></div>
<p><b>Conversion of units</b> is the conversion between different <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Units_of_measurement" title="Units of measurement">units of measurement</a> for the same <a href="/wiki/Quantity" title="Quantity">quantity</a>, typically through multiplicative <b>conversion factors</b>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Techniques">Techniques</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Techniques">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dimensional_analysis" title="Dimensional analysis">Dimensional analysis</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Process_overview">Process overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Process overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The process of conversion depends on the specific situation and the intended purpose.  This may be governed by regulation, <a href="/wiki/Contract" title="Contract">contract</a>,  <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technical_specifications" title="Technical specifications">technical specifications</a> or other published <a href="/wiki/Technical_standard" title="Technical standard">standards</a>.  Engineering judgment may include such factors as:
</p>
<ul><li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precision_and_accuracy" title="Precision and accuracy">precision and accuracy</a> of measurement and the associated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uncertainty_of_measurement" title="Uncertainty of measurement">uncertainty of measurement</a>.</li>
<li>The statistical <a href="/wiki/Confidence_interval" title="Confidence interval">confidence interval</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tolerance_interval" title="Tolerance interval">tolerance interval</a> of the initial measurement.</li>
<li>The number of <a href="/wiki/Significant_figures" title="Significant figures">significant figures</a> of the measurement.</li>
<li>The intended use of the measurement including the <a href="/wiki/Engineering_tolerance" title="Engineering tolerance">engineering tolerances</a>.</li>
<li>Historical definitions of the units and their derivatives used in old measurements; e.g., <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_foot" title="International foot">international foot</a> vs. US <a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)#Survey_foot" title="Foot (unit)">survey foot</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Some conversions from one system of units to another need to be exact, without increasing or decreasing the precision of the first measurement. This is sometimes called <i>soft conversion</i>. It does not involve changing the physical configuration of the item being measured.
</p><p>By contrast, a <i>hard conversion</i> or an <i>adaptive conversion</i>  may not be exactly equivalent. It changes the measurement to convenient and workable numbers and units in the new system. It sometimes involves a slightly different configuration, or size substitution, of the item.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Real_versus_nominal_value" title="Real versus nominal value">Nominal values</a> are sometimes allowed and used.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conversion_factors">Conversion factors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Conversion factors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A conversion factor is used to change the units of a measured quantity without changing its value. The <b>unity bracket method</b> of unit conversion<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BodóJones2013_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-BodóJones2013-1">[1]</a></sup> consists of a fraction in which the denominator is equal to the numerator, but they are in different units.  Because of the identity property of multiplication, the value of a quantity will not change as long as it is multiplied by one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Also, if the numerator and denominator of a fraction are equal to each other, then the fraction is equal to one. So as long as the numerator and denominator of the fraction are equivalent, they will not affect the value of the measured quantity.
</p><p>The following example demonstrates how the unity bracket method is used to convert the rate 5 kilometers per second to meters per second. The symbols km, m, and s represent kilometer, meter, and second, respectively. 
</p><p><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {5{\cancel {\text{km}}}}{\text{s}}}\cdot }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<menclose notation="updiagonalstrike">
<mtext>km</mtext>
</menclose>

<mtext>s</mtext>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\frac {5000{\text{ m}}}{\text{s}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/095d557c9092de6adc9c02070bea595a4d9b63d9" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:8.002ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span>
</p><p>Thus, it is found that 5 kilometers per second is equal to 5000 meters per second.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Software_tools">Software tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Software tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are many conversion tools. They are found in the function libraries of applications such as spreadsheets databases, in calculators, and in macro packages and plugins for many other applications such as the mathematical, scientific and technical applications.
</p><p>There are many standalone applications that offer the thousands of the various units with conversions.  For example, the <a href="/wiki/Free_software_movement" title="Free software movement">free software movement</a> offers a command line utility <a class="external text" href="https://www.gnu.org/software/units/" rel="nofollow">GNU units</a> for Linux and Windows.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tables_of_conversion_factors">Tables of conversion factors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tables of conversion factors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(January 2011)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>This article gives lists of conversion factors for each of a number of physical quantities, which are listed in the index. For each physical quantity, a number of different units (some only of historical interest) are shown and expressed in terms of the corresponding SI unit. Conversions between units in the <a href="/wiki/Metric_system" title="Metric system">metric system</a> are defined by their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SI_prefix" title="SI prefix">prefixes</a> (for example, 1 kilogram = 1000 grams, 1 milligram = 0.001 grams) and are thus not listed in this article. Exceptions are made if the unit is commonly known by another name (for example, 1 micron = 10<sup>−6</sup> metre). Within each table, the units are listed alphabetically, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SI" title="SI">SI</a> units (base or derived) are highlighted.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>Legend
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Symbol

<th>Definition
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th>≡
</th>
<td>exactly equal
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>≈
</th>
<td>approximately equal to
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><var><span style="text-decoration:overline;">digits</span></var>
</th>
<td>indicates that <var>digits</var> repeat infinitely (e.g. <span style="white-space:nowrap">8.294<span style="margin-left:0.25em"><span style="text-decoration:overline;">369</span></span></span> corresponds to <span style="white-space:nowrap">8.294<span style="margin-left:0.25em">369</span><span style="margin-left:0.25em">369</span><span style="margin-left:0.25em">369</span><span style="margin-left:0.25em">369</span><span style="margin-left:0.25em">…</span></span>)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>(H)
</th>
<td>of chiefly historical interest
</td></tr></tbody></table>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass">Mass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Mass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Notes:
</p>
<ul><li>See <a href="/wiki/Weight" title="Weight">Weight</a> for detail of mass/weight distinction and conversion.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avoirdupois" title="Avoirdupois">Avoirdupois</a> is a system of mass based on a pound of 16 ounces, while <a href="/wiki/Troy_weight" title="Troy weight">Troy weight</a> is the system of mass where 12 troy ounces equals one troy pound.</li>
<li>In this table, the unit <i>gee</i> is used to denote <a href="/wiki/Standard_gravity" title="Standard gravity">standard gravity</a> in order to avoid confusion with the "g" symbol for grams.</li></ul>

<td>s
</td>
<td>Time of <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7009919263177000000♠</span>9<span style="margin-left:.25em;">192</span><span style="margin-left:.25em;">631</span><span style="margin-left:.25em;">770</span></span> periods of the radiation corresponding to the transition between the two hyperfine levels of the ground state of the caesium 133 atom at 0 K<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sibaseunits_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-sibaseunits-10">[10]</a></sup> (but other seconds are sometimes used in astronomy). <td colspan="4">
<dl><dt>Note</dt></dl>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-sound-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-sound_38-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-sound_38-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The speed of sound varies especially with temperature and pressure from about <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7002340277777777777♠</span>1225 km/h</span> (761 mph or 661 kn)<br/>in air at sea level to about <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7002295000000000000♠</span>1062 km/h</span> (660 mph or 570 kn) at jet altitudes (<span style="white-space: nowrap">12<span style="margin-left: 0.25em">200</span></span> m or <span style="white-space: nowrap">40<span style="margin-left: 0.25em">000</span></span> ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[32]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Velocity" title="Velocity">velocity</a> consists of a speed combined with a direction; the speed part of the velocity takes units of speed.
</p>

<td>≈ <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7003393887500000000♠</span>3.938<span style="margin-left:.25em;">875</span><span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>3</sup> W</span>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Magnetic_flux_density">Magnetic flux density</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Magnetic flux density">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>What physicists call <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_field" title="Magnetic field">Magnetic field</a> is called <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_flux" title="Magnetic flux">Magnetic flux</a> density by electrical engineers and magnetic induction by applied mathematicians and electrical engineers.
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Name of unit
</th>
<th>Symbol
</th>
<th>Definition
</th>
<th>Relation to SI units
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Gauss_(unit)" title="Gauss (unit)">gauss</a> (CGS unit)</td>
<td>G
</td>
<td>≡ <a href="/wiki/Maxwell_(unit)" title="Maxwell (unit)">Mx</a>/cm<sup>2</sup> = 10<sup>−4</sup> T
</td>
<td>= 10<sup>−4</sup> T <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SI-10_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-SI-10-47">[41]</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr style="background:#dfd;">
<td><a href="/wiki/Tesla_(unit)" title="Tesla (unit)">tesla</a> (SI unit)</td>
<td>T
</td>
<td>≡ <a href="/wiki/Weber_(unit)" title="Weber (unit)">Wb</a>/<a href="/wiki/Square_metre" title="Square metre">m<sup>2</sup></a>
</td>
<td>= 1 T = 1 Wb/m<sup>2</sup> <span class="nowrap">= 1 kg/(A·s<sup>2</sup>)</span>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inductance">Inductance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Inductance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption><a href="/wiki/Inductance" title="Inductance">Inductance</a>
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Name of unit
</th>
<th>Symbol
</th>
<th>Definition
</th>
<th>Relation to SI units
</th></tr>
<tr style="background:#dfd;">
<td><a href="/wiki/Henry_(unit)" title="Henry (unit)">henry</a> (SI unit)</td>
<td>H
</td>
<td>The inductance of a closed circuit that produces one volt of electromotive force when the current in the circuit varies at a uniform rate of one ampere per second.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cipm1946_40-8"><a href="#cite_note-cipm1946-40">[34]</a></sup>
</td>
<td>= 1 H = 1 Wb/A <span class="nowrap">= 1 kg·m<sup>2</sup>/(A·s)<sup>2</sup></span>
</td></tr></tbody></table>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Information_entropy">Information entropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Information entropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable">

</th>

</th>

<td>nat

<td>
</td>

<td>

</td>

<td>
</td>

</td></tr>

<td><a href="/wiki/Kilobyte" title="Kilobyte">kilobyte</a> (decimal)</td>
<td>kB
</td>
<td>≡ <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7003100000000000000♠</span>1000 B</span>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>= <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7003800000000000000♠</span>8000</span> bit
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Kilobyte" title="Kilobyte">kilobyte</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kibibyte" title="Kibibyte">kibibyte</a>)</td>
<td>KB; KiB
</td>
<td>≡ <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7003102400000000000♠</span>1024 B</span>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>= 2<sup>13</sup> bit = <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7003819200000000000♠</span>8192</span> bit
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Modern standards (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISO_80000" title="ISO 80000">ISO 80000</a>) prefer the <a href="/wiki/Shannon_(unit)" title="Shannon (unit)">shannon</a> to the bit as a unit for a quantity of information entropy, whereas the (discrete) storage space of digital devices is measured in bits. Thus, uncompressed redundant data occupy more than one bit of storage per shannon of information entropy. The multiples of a bit listed above are usually used with this meaning.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Luminous_intensity">Luminous intensity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Luminous intensity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The candela is the preferred nomenclature for the SI unit.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption><a href="/wiki/Luminous_intensity" title="Luminous intensity">Luminous intensity</a>
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Name of unit
</th>
<th>Symbol
</th>
<th>Definition
</th>
<th>Relation to SI units
</th></tr>
<tr style="background:#dfd;">
<td><a href="/wiki/Candela" title="Candela">candela</a> (SI base unit); candle
</td>
<td>cd
</td>
<td>The luminous intensity, in a given direction, of a source that emits monochromatic radiation of frequency 540<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">12</span></sup> hertz and that has a radiant intensity in that direction of 1/683 watt per steradian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sibaseunits_10-5"><a href="#cite_note-sibaseunits-10">[10]</a></sup>
</td>
<td>= 1 cd
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Candlepower" title="Candlepower">candlepower</a> (new)
</td>
<td>cp
</td>
<td>≡ cd The use of <i>candlepower</i> as a unit is discouraged due to its ambiguity.
</td>
<td>= 1 cd
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Candlepower" title="Candlepower">candlepower</a> (old, pre-1948)
</td>
<td>cp
</td>
<td>Varies and is poorly reproducible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[42]</a></sup> Approximately 0.981 cd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-howmany_18-6"><a href="#cite_note-howmany-18">[18]</a></sup>
</td>
<td>≈ 0.981 cd
</td></tr></tbody></table>

<h3><span id="Radiation_.E2.80.93_source_activity"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Radiation_–_source_activity">Radiation – source activity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Radiation – source activity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radioactivity" title="Radioactivity">Radioactivity</a>
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Name of unit
</th>
<th>Symbol
</th>
<th>Definition
</th>
<th>Relation to SI units
</th></tr>
<tr style="background:#dfd;">
<td><a href="/wiki/Becquerel" title="Becquerel">becquerel</a> (SI unit)</td>
<td>Bq
</td>
<td>≡ Number of disintegrations per second
</td>
<td>= 1 Bq = 1/s
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Curie" title="Curie">curie</a></td>
<td>Ci
</td>
<td>≡ <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7010370000000000000♠</span>3.7<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>10</sup> Bq</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SP811-2008_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-SP811-2008-49">[43]</a></sup>
</td>
<td>= <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7010370000000000000♠</span>3.7<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>10</sup> Bq</span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Rutherford_(unit)" title="Rutherford (unit)">rutherford</a> (H)</td>
<td>rd
</td>
<td>≡ 1 MBq
</td>
<td>= 10<sup>6</sup> Bq
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Although becquerel (Bq) and hertz (Hz) both ultimately refer to the same SI base unit (s<sup>−1</sup>), Hz is used only for periodic phenomena (ie repetitions at regular intervals), and Bq is only used for stochastic processes (ie at random intervals) associated with radioactivity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sibrochure222_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-sibrochure222-50">[44]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Radiation_.E2.80.93_exposure"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Radiation_–_exposure">Radiation – exposure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Conversion_of_units&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Radiation – exposure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</td>
<td>1 R ≡ <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">6996258000000000000♠</span>2.58<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>−4</sup> C/kg</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nistguide_43-5"><a href="#cite_note-nistguide-43">[37]</a></sup>

<th>Name of unit
</th>
<th>Symbol
</th>
<th>Definition
</th>
<th>Relation to SI units
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C3%B6ntgen_equivalent_man" title="Röntgen equivalent man">Röntgen equivalent man</a></td>
<td>rem
</td>
<td>≡ 0.01 Sv
</td>
<td>= 0.01 Sv
</td></tr>
<tr style="background:#dfd;">
<td><a href="/wiki/Sievert" title="Sievert">sievert</a> (SI unit)</td>
<td>Sv
</td>
<td>≡ 1 J/kg<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sibrochure222_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-sibrochure222-50">[44]</a></sup>
</td>
<td>= 1 Sv
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Although the definitions for sievert (Sv) and gray (Gy) would seem to indicate that they measure the same quantities, this is not the case. The effect of receiving a certain dose of radiation (given as Gy) is variable and depends on many factors, thus a new unit was needed to denote the biological effectiveness of that dose on the body; this is known as the equivalent dose and is shown in Sv. The general relationship between absorbed dose and equivalent dose can be represented as
</p>
<dl><dd><i>H = Q · D</i></dd></dl>
<p>where <i>H</i> is the equivalent dose, <i>D</i> is the absorbed dose, and <i>Q</i> is a dimensionless quality factor. Thus, for any quantity of <i>D</i> measured in Gy, the numerical value for <i>H</i> measured in Sv may be different.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[47]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-sibrochure222-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-sibrochure222_50-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-sibrochure222_50-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070618123613/http://www.bipm.org/en/si/si_brochure/chapter2/2-2/table3.html" rel="nofollow"><i>The International System of Units, Section 2.2.2., Table 3</i></a> (8 ed.), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bureau_International_des_Poids_et_Mesures" title="Bureau International des Poids et Mesures">Bureau International des Poids et Mesures</a>, 2006, archived from <a class="external text" href="http://www.bipm.org/en/si/si_brochure/chapter2/2-2/table3.html" rel="nofollow">the original</a> on June 18, 2007<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 27,</span> 2009</span></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+International+System+of+Units%2C+Section+2.2.2.%2C+Table+3&amp;rft.edition=8&amp;rft.pub=Bureau+International+des+Poids+et+Mesures&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.bipm.org%2Fen%2Fsi%2Fsi_brochure%2Fchapter2%2F2-2%2Ftable3.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AConversion+of+units"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><a class="external text" href="http://physics.nist.gov/Pubs/SP811/sec05.html#5.2" rel="nofollow"><i>The NIST Guide to the SI (Special Publication 811), section 5.2</i></a>, 2008<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 27,</span> 2009</span></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+NIST+Guide+to+the+SI+%28Special+Publication+811%29%2C+section+5.2&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fphysics.nist.gov%2FPubs%2FSP811%2Fsec05.html%235.2&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AConversion+of+units"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>
